## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration–time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time derivative of concentration A, which is the standard form of an ordinary differential equation used to model chemical reaction kinetics. With only (t, A) available, likely models are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where the rate depends on A (reaction order, saturation, equilibrium approach) and possibly explicitly on time (time-varying effective rate constants, forcing, deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- Zeroth-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed/source term into A)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, well-mixed first-order kinetics)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A -> products under mass action)
- General order-n power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (effective reaction order c1 from lumped/empirical kinetics)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplified formation limited by depletion/capacity)
- Saturating (Monod-type) decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by active sites/transport; transitions from first-order to zero-order)
- Inhibited decay (substrate inhibition analogue): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate decreases at high A due to inhibition/aggregation)
- Time-varying first-order rate (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant changes over time due to catalyst aging or environmental drift)
- Time-varying first-order rate (exponential deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (reaction slows as catalyst deactivates exponentially)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) (light/dosing cycles or oscillatory forcing affecting rate)
- Pulse-driven conversion: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * (t - c2)**2) (short activation window such as flash photolysis or pulsed reagent addition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strict consumption-only reactions typically imply dA_dt <= 0 for A >= 0, favoring forms like -f(A,t) with f >= 0.
- Mass-action kinetics often produce polynomial dependence on concentration (A, A**2, A**n); the exponent encodes effective reaction order.
- Approach to equilibrium/steady state is naturally captured by a linear restoring term proportional to (c1 - A).
- Catalyst/site/transport limitation commonly yields saturating rational forms where increasing A no longer increases |dA_dt| beyond a maximum.
- Self-acceleration (autocatalysis) is suggested by multiplicative A factors (rate ∝ A at low A), often combined with a limiting factor (c1 - A).
- If experimental rate slows over time at fixed A, consider explicit time dependence in the effective rate constant (c0 + c1*t, exp(-c*t), 1/(1+c*t)).
- Periodic experimental protocols (light chopping, dosing) often appear as sinusoidal modulation multiplying a baseline rate term.
- Transient activations (pulses) are well represented by Gaussian-in-time or other localized time envelopes multiplying A-dependent kinetics.
